{"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01QPj9DC2KXt5q7udfL8DoPi","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_01MUVvFrPn5qPahFCTh1ipFe","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/workspace/documentation.md","content":"# VS Code Diagnostic API Reference\n\n## Overview\n\nThe Diagnostic API allows VS Code extensions to report code issues to users. Diagnostics represent problems such as compilation errors, linting violations, or other code quality concerns. Each diagnostic is associated with a specific location in a document and includes a severity level, message, and optional metadata.\n\nThe API is accessed through the `vscode.languages` namespace and provides:\n- **Diagnostic**: A class representing a single diagnostic issue\n- **DiagnosticCollection**: A container for managing diagnostics across documents\n- **DiagnosticSeverity**: An enum for severity levels\n- **DiagnosticRelatedInformation**: Additional context for diagnostics\n- **DiagnosticTag**: Metadata tags for categorizing diagnostics\n- **Functions**: Factory functions and query methods\n- **Events**: Notifications when diagnostics change\n\n---\n\n## Core Types\n\n### DiagnosticSeverity\n\nAn enumeration that defines the severity levels for diagnostics.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticSeverity {\n    Error = 0,\n    Warning = 1,\n    Information = 2,\n    Hint = 3\n}\n```\n\n**Values:**\n\n- **Error** (0): Something not allowed by the rules of a language or other means. Displayed prominently in red.\n- **Warning** (1): Something suspicious but allowed. Displayed in yellow/orange.\n- **Information** (2): Something to inform about but not a problem. Displayed in blue.\n- **Hint** (3): Something to hint at a better way of doing it, like proposing a refactoring. Displayed subtly.\n\n**Usage Notes:**\n- The default severity for a diagnostic is `Error` if not specified in the constructor\n- Severity affects visual styling in the editor (colors, icons, gutter decorations)\n- Severity is also used to organize diagnostics in the Problems panel\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticTag\n\nAn enumeration for additional metadata about the type of a diagnostic.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticTag {\n    Unnecessary = 1,\n    Deprecated = 2\n}\n```\n\n**Values:**\n\n- **Unnecessary** (1): Unused or unnecessary code. Diagnostics with this tag are rendered faded out. The amount of fading is controlled by the `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.opacity\"` theme color. For high contrast themes, the `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.border\"` theme color is used to underline unnecessary code instead of fading it out.\n\n- **Deprecated** (2): Deprecated or obsolete code. Diagnostics with this tag are rendered with a strike through.\n\n**Usage Notes:**\n- Tags are optional and specified via the `tags` property on a Diagnostic\n- Multiple tags can be applied to a single diagnostic as an array\n- Tags only affect rendering; they don't change diagnostic behavior\n- Tags are particularly useful for refactoring and cleanup workflows\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new Diagnostic(range, \"Unused variable\", DiagnosticSeverity.Warning);\ndiagnostic.tags = [DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\n```\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticRelatedInformation\n\nA class representing related diagnostic information that provides additional context for a diagnostic.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport class DiagnosticRelatedInformation {\n    location: Location;\n    message: string;\n\n    constructor(location: Location, message: string);\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n- **location: Location** - The location of this related diagnostic information. Must be a valid Location object containing a URI and Range.\n- **message: string** - The message describing the related information.\n\n**Constructor:**\n```typescript\nconstructor(location: Location, message: string)\n```\n\nCreates a new DiagnosticRelatedInformation object with the provided location and message.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `location` (Location): The location where the related information points to\n- `message` (string): A human-readable message describing the relationship\n\n**Usage Notes:**\n- Used to point to related code locations that cause or relate to a diagnostic\n- Common use case: when duplicating a symbol in a scope, link both definitions together\n- Related information is displayed in the editor as secondary messages/links\n- Each Diagnostic can have multiple related information items in its `relatedInformation` array\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\n// Mark duplicate symbol location\nconst related = new DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n    new Location(uri, range),\n    \"First declaration of symbol 'foo'\"\n);\ndiagnostic.relatedInformation = [related];\n```\n\n---\n\n### Diagnostic\n\nA class representing a diagnostic issue such as a compiler error or linting warning.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport class Diagnostic {\n    range: Range;\n    message: string;\n    severity: DiagnosticSeverity;\n    source?: string;\n    code?: string | number | {\n        value: string | number;\n        target: Uri;\n    };\n    relatedInformation?: DiagnosticRelatedInformation[];\n    tags?: DiagnosticTag[];\n\n    constructor(range: Range, message: string, severity?: DiagnosticSeverity);\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n- **range: Range** - The range to which this diagnostic applies. Must be a valid Range object. The range is used to highlight the problematic code in the editor.\n\n- **message: string** - The human-readable message describing the issue. This message is displayed in the Problems panel and in hover tooltips.\n\n- **severity: DiagnosticSeverity** - The severity level of this diagnostic. Default is `DiagnosticSeverity.Error` if not set in the constructor. Affects visual styling and organization.\n\n- **source?: string** (optional) - A human-readable string describing the source of this diagnostic, e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint', or 'super-lint'. Displayed in the Problems panel alongside the message.\n\n- **code?: string | number | { value: string | number; target: Uri }** (optional) - A code or identifier for this diagnostic. Can be:\n  - A simple string or number identifier (e.g., \"E001\")\n  - An object with:\n    - `value`: The code identifier\n    - `target`: A URI to open with more information (e.g., documentation link)\n\n  Used for later processing, e.g., when providing Code Actions via CodeActionContext.\n\n- **relatedInformation?: DiagnosticRelatedInformation[]** (optional) - An array of DiagnosticRelatedInformation objects that provide additional context. Used to point to related code locations or definitions.\n\n- **tags?: DiagnosticTag[]** (optional) - An array of DiagnosticTag values for additional metadata about the diagnostic. Affects visual rendering only.\n\n**Constructor:**\n```typescript\nconstructor(range: Range, message: string, severity?: DiagnosticSeverity)\n```\n\nCreates a new Diagnostic object with the specified range, message, and optional severity.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `range` (Range): The range to which this diagnostic applies. Required.\n- `message` (string): A human-readable message describing the issue. Required.\n- `severity` (DiagnosticSeverity, optional): The severity level. Default is `DiagnosticSeverity.Error`.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Diagnostics are only valid within the scope of a file\n- A Diagnostic object is immutable after properties are set through the collection\n- The range can be any valid Range, including zero-width ranges\n- Messages should be concise but descriptive\n- Source strings are used by VS Code for filtering and organization\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new Diagnostic(\n    new Range(0, 0, 0, 10),\n    \"Unexpected token\",\n    DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n);\ndiagnostic.source = \"typescript\";\ndiagnostic.code = {\n    value: \"TS1005\",\n    target: Uri.parse(\"https://www.typescriptlang.org/docs/handbook/release-notes/typescript-3-0.html\")\n};\n```\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticChangeEvent\n\nAn interface representing an event that fires when diagnostics change globally.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport interface DiagnosticChangeEvent {\n    readonly uris: readonly Uri[];\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n- **uris: readonly Uri[]** - An array of resources (URIs) for which diagnostics have changed. These can be new diagnostics, updated diagnostics, or cleared diagnostics.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Fired when diagnostics are added, removed, or modified via any DiagnosticCollection\n- The URIs array contains only resources where changes occurred\n- An empty or missing resource in a change means all diagnostics for that resource were cleared\n- Event is fired even if the actual diagnostic content is the same but the collection reference changed\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticCollection\n\nAn interface representing a container for managing diagnostics for specific documents.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport interface DiagnosticCollection extends Iterable<[uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[]]> {\n    readonly name: string;\n\n    set(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void;\n    set(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void;\n\n    delete(uri: Uri): void;\n    clear(): void;\n\n    forEach(callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any, thisArg?: any): void;\n\n    get(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined;\n    has(uri: Uri): boolean;\n\n    dispose(): void;\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n- **name: string** (readonly) - The name of this diagnostic collection, e.g., 'typescript' or 'eslint'. Every diagnostic from this collection will be associated with this name. The task framework uses this name when defining problem matchers.\n\n**Methods:**\n\n#### set(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void\n\nAssign diagnostics for a given resource, replacing existing diagnostics for that resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri` (Uri): A resource identifier (typically a file URI)\n- `diagnostics` (readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): Array of diagnostics or `undefined` to clear all diagnostics for this resource\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Replaces all existing diagnostics for the URI\n- Passing `undefined` clears all diagnostics for the URI\n- Passing an empty array `[]` also clears diagnostics\n- Fires `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event with the URI in the change event\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-linter');\nconst diagnostics = [\n    new Diagnostic(range1, \"Error 1\", DiagnosticSeverity.Error),\n    new Diagnostic(range2, \"Warning 1\", DiagnosticSeverity.Warning)\n];\ncollection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n```\n\n#### set(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void\n\nReplace diagnostics for multiple resources in this collection.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `entries` (ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): An array of tuples where each tuple contains a URI and its diagnostics, or `undefined`\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Multiple tuples of the same URI will be merged. For example, `[[file1, [d1]], [file1, [d2]]]` is equivalent to `[[file1, [d1, d2]]]`\n- If a diagnostics item is `undefined` as in `[file1, undefined]`, all previous diagnostics for that URI are removed but subsequent entries for that URI in the array are still processed\n- Fires `onDidChangeDiagnostics` once with all changed URIs\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.set([\n    [fileUri1, [diagnostic1, diagnostic2]],\n    [fileUri2, [diagnostic3, diagnostic4, diagnostic5]]\n]);\n```\n\n#### delete(uri: Uri): void\n\nRemove all diagnostics from this collection that belong to the provided URI.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri` (Uri): A resource identifier\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Equivalent to `set(uri, undefined)`\n- Fires `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event with the URI\n- If the URI has no diagnostics, nothing happens (no error)\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.delete(document.uri);\n```\n\n#### clear(): void\n\nRemove all diagnostics from this collection across all resources.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Equivalent to calling `set(undefined)` (which is not directly callable but represents the intent)\n- Fires `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event for all previously-diagnosed URIs\n- After clear, the collection is empty\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.clear();\n```\n\n#### forEach(callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any, thisArg?: any): void\n\nIterate over each entry in this collection.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `callback` (function): Function to execute for each entry with signature `(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any`\n- `thisArg` (optional): The `this` context used when invoking the handler function\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Called once for each URI that has diagnostics in the collection\n- Iteration order is not guaranteed\n- The callback receives the URI, its diagnostics (immutable array), and a reference to the collection\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.forEach((uri, diagnostics, collection) => {\n    console.log(`${uri.toString()}: ${diagnostics.length} diagnostics`);\n});\n```\n\n#### get(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined\n\nGet the diagnostics for a given resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri` (Uri): A resource identifier\n\n**Returns:**\n- An immutable array of Diagnostic objects if diagnostics exist for the URI, or `undefined` if none exist\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns an immutable/readonly array; modifications to the returned array do not affect the collection\n- Returns `undefined` (not an empty array) if no diagnostics exist for the URI\n- Safe to call even if the URI has not been set in the collection\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = collection.get(document.uri);\nif (diagnostics) {\n    console.log(`Found ${diagnostics.length} diagnostics`);\n    for (const diag of diagnostics) {\n        console.log(diag.message);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### has(uri: Uri): boolean\n\nCheck if this collection contains diagnostics for a given resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri` (Uri): A resource identifier\n\n**Returns:**\n- `true` if the collection has diagnostics for the URI, `false` otherwise\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Does not count zero-width ranges or other special cases\n- Returns `true` even if the diagnostics array is empty (if it was explicitly set)\n- Returns `false` if the URI has never been set or has been cleared\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nif (collection.has(document.uri)) {\n    const diagnostics = collection.get(document.uri);\n    // Process diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n#### dispose(): void\n\nDispose and free associated resources.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Calls `clear()` internally\n- Removes all diagnostics from the collection\n- After disposal, the collection should not be used\n- Typically called during extension deactivation\n- Fires `onDidChangeDiagnostics` for all previously-diagnosed URIs\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncontext.subscriptions.push(collection); // Auto-dispose when extension deactivates\n// Later:\ncollection.dispose(); // Manual disposal\n```\n\n**Iteration:**\n\nDiagnosticCollection implements Iterable, so it can be used with `for...of`:\n\n```typescript\nfor (const [uri, diagnostics] of collection) {\n    console.log(`${uri.toString()}: ${diagnostics.length} issues`);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Functions\n\n### createDiagnosticCollection(name?: string): DiagnosticCollection\n\nCreates a new diagnostic collection.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport function createDiagnosticCollection(name?: string): DiagnosticCollection\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `name` (string, optional): The name of the collection, e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint', 'my-linter'. Used for grouping and filtering in the Problems panel.\n\n**Returns:**\n- A new DiagnosticCollection instance\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Creates an empty collection\n- The collection name is visible in the Problems panel\n- Each extension should typically create one collection per feature or linter\n- Collections are independent; clearing one doesn't affect others\n- Should be stored and disposed in extension lifecycle\n\n**Error Handling:**\n- No errors thrown; even invalid names are accepted (though empty names are not recommended)\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnosticCollection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-extension');\ncontext.subscriptions.push(diagnosticCollection); // Auto-dispose on deactivation\n```\n\n---\n\n### getDiagnostics(resource: Uri): Diagnostic[]\n\nGet all diagnostics for a given resource from all collections.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport function getDiagnostics(resource: Uri): Diagnostic[]\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `resource` (Uri): A resource URI\n\n**Returns:**\n- An array of Diagnostic objects from all collections for the given resource, or an empty array if none exist\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns diagnostics from ALL diagnostic collections (not just one)\n- Returns an empty array (never undefined) if no diagnostics exist\n- The returned array is a copy, not a reference to internal state\n- Diagnostics are returned in an arbitrary order\n- Includes diagnostics from the built-in collections and all extension collections\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst allDiagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(document.uri);\nconsole.log(`Total diagnostics: ${allDiagnostics.length}`);\n\nfor (const diag of allDiagnostics) {\n    console.log(`${diag.source}: ${diag.message}`);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### getDiagnostics(): [Uri, Diagnostic[]][]\n\nGet all diagnostics from all collections.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport function getDiagnostics(): [Uri, Diagnostic[]][]\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- None\n\n**Returns:**\n- An array of tuples, each containing a URI and its associated diagnostics, or an empty array\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns diagnostics from ALL collections across ALL resources\n- Returns an empty array (never undefined) if no diagnostics exist\n- The returned array is a copy of internal state\n- Each URI appears at most once in the result\n- Useful for bulk operations or diagnostics overview\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst allDiagnosticsEverywhere = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics();\nconsole.log(`Total resources with diagnostics: ${allDiagnosticsEverywhere.length}`);\n\nlet totalDiagnostics = 0;\nfor (const [uri, diagnostics] of allDiagnosticsEverywhere) {\n    totalDiagnostics += diagnostics.length;\n    console.log(`${uri.toString()}: ${diagnostics.length} diagnostics`);\n}\nconsole.log(`Total diagnostics: ${totalDiagnostics}`);\n```\n\n---\n\n## Events\n\n### onDidChangeDiagnostics: Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>\n\nAn event which fires when the global set of diagnostics changes.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport const onDidChangeDiagnostics: Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>\n```\n\n**Type:**\n- `Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>`\n\n**Event Parameter:**\n- `DiagnosticChangeEvent.uris`: Array of URIs where diagnostics changed\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Fired whenever diagnostics are added, removed, or modified via any DiagnosticCollection\n- Fired once per change operation, even if multiple URIs are affected\n- The event includes only the URIs that changed, not the actual diagnostic content\n- Fired by both the user's collections and built-in collections (TypeScript, etc.)\n- Listeners can query current diagnostics using `getDiagnostics()` if needed\n\n**Usage Notes:**\n- Use this to update UI that depends on the current diagnostics state\n- Avoid expensive operations in event handlers; use debouncing if necessary\n- The event URI list may be empty in some edge cases\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nvscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(event => {\n    console.log(`Diagnostics changed for ${event.uris.length} files`);\n\n    for (const uri of event.uris) {\n        const diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n        console.log(`${uri.toString()}: ${diagnostics.length} issues`);\n    }\n});\n```\n\n---\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Basic Example: Creating and Publishing Diagnostics\n\nThis example shows how to create a simple linter that validates JSON files:\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    // Create a diagnostic collection\n    const diagnosticCollection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('json-validator');\n    context.subscriptions.push(diagnosticCollection);\n\n    // Listen to document changes\n    vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(event => {\n        const document = event.document;\n\n        // Only validate JSON files\n        if (document.languageId !== 'json') {\n            return;\n        }\n\n        const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n\n        try {\n            JSON.parse(document.getText());\n        } catch (error) {\n            // Create a diagnostic for the parse error\n            const message = error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Invalid JSON';\n            const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n                new vscode.Range(0, 0, 0, 1),\n                message,\n                vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n            );\n            diagnostic.source = 'json-validator';\n            diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n        }\n\n        // Publish diagnostics for this file\n        diagnosticCollection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n    }, null, context.subscriptions);\n\n    // Clear diagnostics when document is closed\n    vscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(document => {\n        diagnosticCollection.delete(document.uri);\n    }, null, context.subscriptions);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Advanced Example: Multiple Issue Types and Related Information\n\nThis example shows a more sophisticated linter with multiple diagnostic types and related information:\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\ninterface LintIssue {\n    line: number;\n    column: number;\n    length: number;\n    severity: vscode.DiagnosticSeverity;\n    code: string;\n    message: string;\n    relatedInfo?: { line: number; column: number; length: number; message: string };\n}\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-linter');\n    context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n    function lintDocument(document: vscode.TextDocument) {\n        const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n        const issues = performLinting(document); // Your custom linting logic\n\n        for (const issue of issues) {\n            const range = new vscode.Range(\n                issue.line, issue.column,\n                issue.line, issue.column + issue.length\n            );\n\n            const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n                range,\n                issue.message,\n                issue.severity\n            );\n            diagnostic.source = 'my-linter';\n            diagnostic.code = {\n                value: issue.code,\n                target: vscode.Uri.parse(`https://docs.example.com/rules/${issue.code}`)\n            };\n\n            // Add related information if available\n            if (issue.relatedInfo) {\n                const relatedRange = new vscode.Range(\n                    issue.relatedInfo.line, issue.relatedInfo.column,\n                    issue.relatedInfo.line, issue.relatedInfo.column + issue.relatedInfo.length\n                );\n                diagnostic.relatedInformation = [\n                    new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n                        new vscode.Location(document.uri, relatedRange),\n                        issue.relatedInfo.message\n                    )\n                ];\n            }\n\n            // Mark unused code\n            if (issue.code === 'unused-var') {\n                diagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\n            }\n\n            diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n        }\n\n        collection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n    }\n\n    // Lint on document open and change\n    vscode.workspace.onDidOpenTextDocument(lintDocument, null, context.subscriptions);\n    vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(event => {\n        lintDocument(event.document);\n    }, null, context.subscriptions);\n\n    // Clean up on close\n    vscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(doc => {\n        collection.delete(doc.uri);\n    }, null, context.subscriptions);\n}\n\nfunction performLinting(document: vscode.TextDocument): LintIssue[] {\n    // Your custom linting implementation\n    return [];\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Real-World Pattern: Throttled Linting with Disposables\n\nThis pattern, used in VS Code's built-in extensions, shows how to handle throttling and proper resource cleanup:\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport class ExtensionLinter {\n    private readonly diagnosticsCollection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection;\n    private readonly disposables: vscode.Disposable[] = [];\n    private lintTimer: NodeJS.Timeout | undefined;\n\n    constructor() {\n        this.diagnosticsCollection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('extension-linter');\n        this.disposables.push(this.diagnosticsCollection);\n\n        // Listen to document changes with debouncing\n        vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(\n            event => this.queueLint(event.document),\n            null,\n            this.disposables\n        );\n\n        vscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(\n            document => this.diagnosticsCollection.delete(document.uri),\n            null,\n            this.disposables\n        );\n    }\n\n    private queueLint(document: vscode.TextDocument) {\n        // Clear existing timer\n        if (this.lintTimer) {\n            clearTimeout(this.lintTimer);\n        }\n        // Debounce: wait 300ms after last change before linting\n        this.lintTimer = setTimeout(() => {\n            this.lint(document);\n        }, 300);\n    }\n\n    private async lint(document: vscode.TextDocument) {\n        const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n\n        try {\n            // Perform async linting\n            const issues = await this.lintDocument(document);\n\n            for (const issue of issues) {\n                const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n                    issue.range,\n                    issue.message,\n                    issue.severity\n                );\n                diagnostic.source = 'extension-linter';\n                diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n            }\n        } catch (error) {\n            console.error('Linting error:', error);\n        }\n\n        // Publish all diagnostics at once\n        this.diagnosticsCollection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n    }\n\n    private async lintDocument(document: vscode.TextDocument): Promise<vscode.Diagnostic[]> {\n        // Your linting implementation\n        return [];\n    }\n\n    public dispose() {\n        if (this.lintTimer) {\n            clearTimeout(this.lintTimer);\n        }\n        this.disposables.forEach(d => d.dispose());\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Pattern: Bulk Update with Multiple Files\n\nThis example demonstrates updating diagnostics for multiple files at once:\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport async function runFullProjectLint(\n    collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection,\n    workspacePath: string\n): Promise<void> {\n    const updates: Array<[vscode.Uri, vscode.Diagnostic[] | undefined]> = [];\n\n    // Scan all files in workspace\n    const files = await vscode.workspace.findFiles('**/*.js');\n\n    for (const fileUri of files) {\n        const document = await vscode.workspace.openTextDocument(fileUri);\n        const diagnostics = await lintFile(document);\n        updates.push([fileUri, diagnostics]);\n    }\n\n    // Apply all updates at once (more efficient than individual set() calls)\n    collection.set(updates);\n}\n\nasync function lintFile(document: vscode.TextDocument): Promise<vscode.Diagnostic[]> {\n    // Your linting implementation\n    return [];\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Pattern: Integration with Code Actions\n\nThis example shows how diagnostics work with Code Actions to provide fixes:\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport class MyCodeActionProvider implements vscode.CodeActionProvider {\n    constructor(private diagnosticsCollection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection) {}\n\n    provideCodeActions(\n        document: vscode.TextDocument,\n        range: vscode.Range | vscode.Selection,\n        context: vscode.CodeActionContext\n    ): vscode.CodeAction[] {\n        const actions: vscode.CodeAction[] = [];\n\n        // Get diagnostics from our collection for this range\n        const diagnostics = this.diagnosticsCollection.get(document.uri) || [];\n\n        for (const diagnostic of diagnostics) {\n            if (!diagnostic.range.intersection(range)) {\n                continue;\n            }\n\n            // Only handle certain codes\n            if (typeof diagnostic.code === 'string' && diagnostic.code === 'unused-var') {\n                const action = new vscode.CodeAction(\n                    'Remove unused variable',\n                    vscode.CodeActionKind.QuickFix\n                );\n                action.diagnostics = [diagnostic];\n\n                const edit = new vscode.WorkspaceEdit();\n                // Apply a fix (simplified example)\n                edit.delete(document.uri, diagnostic.range);\n                action.edit = edit;\n\n                actions.push(action);\n            }\n        }\n\n        return actions;\n    }\n\n    static register(\n        context: vscode.ExtensionContext,\n        diagnosticsCollection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection\n    ): void {\n        const provider = new MyCodeActionProvider(diagnosticsCollection);\n        context.subscriptions.push(\n            vscode.languages.registerCodeActionsProvider(\n                { scheme: 'file', language: 'javascript' },\n                provider\n            )\n        );\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Pattern: Listening to Diagnostic Changes\n\nThis pattern shows how to react to diagnostic changes globally:\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    // Monitor all diagnostics changes\n    vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(event => {\n        for (const uri of event.uris) {\n            const diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n            const errorCount = diagnostics.filter(\n                d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n            ).length;\n            const warningCount = diagnostics.filter(\n                d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n            ).length;\n\n            if (errorCount > 0 || warningCount > 0) {\n                console.log(`${uri.toString()}: ${errorCount} errors, ${warningCount} warnings`);\n            }\n        }\n    }, null, context.subscriptions);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Common Patterns\n\n### Resource Lifecycle Management\n\n**Collection Creation and Disposal:**\n```typescript\n// Create and auto-dispose with context\nconst collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-linter');\ncontext.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n// Later, manual disposal if needed\ncollection.dispose();\n```\n\n**File Cleanup:**\n```typescript\nvscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(doc => {\n    collection.delete(doc.uri);\n});\n```\n\n### Diagnostic Filtering and Aggregation\n\n**Count diagnostics by severity:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\nconst errors = diagnostics.filter(d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error).length;\nconst warnings = diagnostics.filter(d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning).length;\n```\n\n**Find all diagnostics in workspace:**\n```typescript\nconst allDiags = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics();\nfor (const [uri, diagnostics] of allDiags) {\n    // Process each URI and its diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n### Batch Updates\n\n**More efficient than multiple set() calls:**\n```typescript\nconst updates: Array<[vscode.Uri, vscode.Diagnostic[] | undefined]> = [];\nfor (const uri of uris) {\n    updates.push([uri, getDiagnosticsFor(uri)]);\n}\ncollection.set(updates);\n```\n\n### Diagnostic Enrichment\n\n**Add metadata and links to diagnostics:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, message);\ndiagnostic.source = 'my-linter';\ndiagnostic.code = {\n    value: 'E001',\n    target: vscode.Uri.parse('https://example.com/rules/E001')\n};\ndiagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\ndiagnostic.relatedInformation = [\n    new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n        new vscode.Location(uri, relatedRange),\n        'Related issue'\n    )\n];\n```\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Common Error Scenarios\n\n**Invalid Range:**\n- If you provide a Range that extends beyond the document bounds, VS Code will clamp it silently. No error is thrown.\n\n**Invalid URI:**\n- Passing invalid URIs may cause silent failures. Always validate URIs before use.\n\n**Undefined vs Empty Array:**\n- `set(uri, undefined)` clears diagnostics\n- `set(uri, [])` also clears diagnostics\n- `get(uri)` returns `undefined` if no diagnostics exist\n\n**Collection After Dispose:**\n- Using a disposed collection may cause errors or silent failures\n- Always check if the extension is still active before using collections\n\n### Safe Patterns\n\n**Always check before accessing:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = collection.get(uri);\nif (diagnostics && diagnostics.length > 0) {\n    // Safe to iterate\n}\n```\n\n**Handle missing resources gracefully:**\n```typescript\nif (collection.has(uri)) {\n    // Resource has diagnostics\n} else {\n    // Resource has no diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n**Proper cleanup on error:**\n```typescript\ntry {\n    // Perform linting\n    collection.set(uri, diagnostics);\n} catch (error) {\n    console.error('Failed to set diagnostics:', error);\n    collection.delete(uri); // Clean up\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Performance Considerations\n\n### Best Practices\n\n1. **Debounce linting**: Use timers to avoid linting on every keystroke\n2. **Batch updates**: Use `set(entries)` instead of multiple `set(uri, ...)` calls\n3. **Lazy linting**: Lint only open files or files with unsaved changes\n4. **Clear unused diagnostics**: Delete diagnostics for closed files promptly\n5. **Limit message length**: Keep diagnostic messages concise to reduce memory usage\n\n### Avoid\n\n- Creating multiple collections for the same linter\n- Linting synchronously on every document change\n- Storing references to diagnostics outside collections\n- Forgetting to dispose collections on deactivation\n\n---\n\n## Related APIs\n\n- **CodeAction**: Used to provide fixes for diagnostics\n- **CodeActionContext**: Includes diagnostics that triggered the code action request\n- **TextDocument**: Source of diagnostic issues\n- **Range**: Specifies the location of a diagnostic\n- **Uri**: Identifies the file associated with a diagnostic\n- **Event**: Used for `onDidChangeDiagnostics` subscription\n\n---\n\n## API Stability\n\nThe Diagnostic API is part of the stable VS Code API and is maintained for backward compatibility. No breaking changes are expected in future releases.\n\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":12,"cache_creation_input_tokens":4190,"cache_read_input_tokens":72582,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":4190},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"f6b0f9e2-35ec-4110-8e6a-6fe6ccd3229d","uuid":"e295e358-2de8-4207-bffc-9ca36f160362"}

Diagnostics represent problems such as compilation errors, linting violations, or other code quality concerns. Each diagnostic is associated with a specific location in a document and includes a severity level, message, and optional metadata.\n\nThe API is accessed through the `vscode.languages` namespace and provides:\n- **Diagnostic**: A class representing a single diagnostic issue\n- **DiagnosticCollection**: A container for managing diagnostics across documents\n- **DiagnosticSeverity**: An enum for severity levels\n- **DiagnosticRelatedInformation**: Additional context for diagnostics\n- **DiagnosticTag**: Metadata tags for categorizing diagnostics\n- **Functions**: Factory functions and query methods\n- **Events**: Notifications when diagnostics change\n\n---\n\n## Core Types\n\n### DiagnosticSeverity\n\nAn enumeration that defines the severity levels for diagnostics.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticSeverity {\n    Error = 0,\n    Warning = 1,\n    Information = 2,\n    Hint = 3\n}\n```\n\n**Values:**\n\n- **Error** (0): Something not allowed by the rules of a language or other means. Displayed prominently in red.\n- **Warning** (1): Something suspicious but allowed. Displayed in yellow/orange.\n- **Information** (2): Something to inform about but not a problem. Displayed in blue.\n- **Hint** (3): Something to hint at a better way of doing it, like proposing a refactoring. Displayed subtly.\n\n**Usage Notes:**\n- The default severity for a diagnostic is `Error` if not specified in the constructor\n- Severity affects visual styling in the editor (colors, icons, gutter decorations)\n- Severity is also used to organize diagnostics in the Problems panel\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticTag\n\nAn enumeration for additional metadata about the type of a diagnostic.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport enum DiagnosticTag {\n    Unnecessary = 1,\n    Deprecated = 2\n}\n```\n\n**Values:**\n\n- **Unnecessary** (1): Unused or unnecessary code. Diagnostics with this tag are rendered faded out. The amount of fading is controlled by the `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.opacity\"` theme color. For high contrast themes, the `\"editorUnnecessaryCode.border\"` theme color is used to underline unnecessary code instead of fading it out.\n\n- **Deprecated** (2): Deprecated or obsolete code. Diagnostics with this tag are rendered with a strike through.\n\n**Usage Notes:**\n- Tags are optional and specified via the `tags` property on a Diagnostic\n- Multiple tags can be applied to a single diagnostic as an array\n- Tags only affect rendering; they don't change diagnostic behavior\n- Tags are particularly useful for refactoring and cleanup workflows\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new Diagnostic(range, \"Unused variable\", DiagnosticSeverity.Warning);\ndiagnostic.tags = [DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\n```\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticRelatedInformation\n\nA class representing related diagnostic information that provides additional context for a diagnostic.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport class DiagnosticRelatedInformation {\n    location: Location;\n    message: string;\n\n    constructor(location: Location, message: string);\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n- **location: Location** - The location of this related diagnostic information. Must be a valid Location object containing a URI and Range.\n- **message: string** - The message describing the related information.\n\n**Constructor:**\n```typescript\nconstructor(location: Location, message: string)\n```\n\nCreates a new DiagnosticRelatedInformation object with the provided location and message.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `location` (Location): The location where the related information points to\n- `message` (string): A human-readable message describing the relationship\n\n**Usage Notes:**\n- Used to point to related code locations that cause or relate to a diagnostic\n- Common use case: when duplicating a symbol in a scope, link both definitions together\n- Related information is displayed in the editor as secondary messages/links\n- Each Diagnostic can have multiple related information items in its `relatedInformation` array\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\n// Mark duplicate symbol location\nconst related = new DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n    new Location(uri, range),\n    \"First declaration of symbol 'foo'\"\n);\ndiagnostic.relatedInformation = [related];\n```\n\n---\n\n### Diagnostic\n\nA class representing a diagnostic issue such as a compiler error or linting warning.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport class Diagnostic {\n    range: Range;\n    message: string;\n    severity: DiagnosticSeverity;\n    source?: string;\n    code?: string | number | {\n        value: string | number;\n        target: Uri;\n    };\n    relatedInformation?: DiagnosticRelatedInformation[];\n    tags?: DiagnosticTag[];\n\n    constructor(range: Range, message: string, severity?: DiagnosticSeverity);\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n- **range: Range** - The range to which this diagnostic applies. Must be a valid Range object. The range is used to highlight the problematic code in the editor.\n\n- **message: string** - The human-readable message describing the issue. This message is displayed in the Problems panel and in hover tooltips.\n\n- **severity: DiagnosticSeverity** - The severity level of this diagnostic. Default is `DiagnosticSeverity.Error` if not set in the constructor. Affects visual styling and organization.\n\n- **source?: string** (optional) - A human-readable string describing the source of this diagnostic, e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint', or 'super-lint'. Displayed in the Problems panel alongside the message.\n\n- **code?: string | number | { value: string | number; target: Uri }** (optional) - A code or identifier for this diagnostic. Can be:\n  - A simple string or number identifier (e.g., \"E001\")\n  - An object with:\n    - `value`: The code identifier\n    - `target`: A URI to open with more information (e.g., documentation link)\n\n  Used for later processing, e.g., when providing Code Actions via CodeActionContext.\n\n- **relatedInformation?: DiagnosticRelatedInformation[]** (optional) - An array of DiagnosticRelatedInformation objects that provide additional context. Used to point to related code locations or definitions.\n\n- **tags?: DiagnosticTag[]** (optional) - An array of DiagnosticTag values for additional metadata about the diagnostic. Affects visual rendering only.\n\n**Constructor:**\n```typescript\nconstructor(range: Range, message: string, severity?: DiagnosticSeverity)\n```\n\nCreates a new Diagnostic object with the specified range, message, and optional severity.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `range` (Range): The range to which this diagnostic applies. Required.\n- `message` (string): A human-readable message describing the issue. Required.\n- `severity` (DiagnosticSeverity, optional): The severity level. Default is `DiagnosticSeverity.Error`.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Diagnostics are only valid within the scope of a file\n- A Diagnostic object is immutable after properties are set through the collection\n- The range can be any valid Range, including zero-width ranges\n- Messages should be concise but descriptive\n- Source strings are used by VS Code for filtering and organization\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new Diagnostic(\n    new Range(0, 0, 0, 10),\n    \"Unexpected token\",\n    DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n);\ndiagnostic.source = \"typescript\";\ndiagnostic.code = {\n    value: \"TS1005\",\n    target: Uri.parse(\"https://www.typescriptlang.org/docs/handbook/release-notes/typescript-3-0.html\")\n};\n```\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticChangeEvent\n\nAn interface representing an event that fires when diagnostics change globally.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport interface DiagnosticChangeEvent {\n    readonly uris: readonly Uri[];\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n- **uris: readonly Uri[]** - An array of resources (URIs) for which diagnostics have changed. These can be new diagnostics, updated diagnostics, or cleared diagnostics.\n\n**Behavior Notes:**\n- Fired when diagnostics are added, removed, or modified via any DiagnosticCollection\n- The URIs array contains only resources where changes occurred\n- An empty or missing resource in a change means all diagnostics for that resource were cleared\n- Event is fired even if the actual diagnostic content is the same but the collection reference changed\n\n---\n\n### DiagnosticCollection\n\nAn interface representing a container for managing diagnostics for specific documents.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport interface DiagnosticCollection extends Iterable<[uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[]]> {\n    readonly name: string;\n\n    set(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void;\n    set(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void;\n\n    delete(uri: Uri): void;\n    clear(): void;\n\n    forEach(callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any, thisArg?: any): void;\n\n    get(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined;\n    has(uri: Uri): boolean;\n\n    dispose(): void;\n}\n```\n\n**Properties:**\n\n- **name: string** (readonly) - The name of this diagnostic collection, e.g., 'typescript' or 'eslint'. Every diagnostic from this collection will be associated with this name. The task framework uses this name when defining problem matchers.\n\n**Methods:**\n\n#### set(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): void\n\nAssign diagnostics for a given resource, replacing existing diagnostics for that resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri` (Uri): A resource identifier (typically a file URI)\n- `diagnostics` (readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined): Array of diagnostics or `undefined` to clear all diagnostics for this resource\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Replaces all existing diagnostics for the URI\n- Passing `undefined` clears all diagnostics for the URI\n- Passing an empty array `[]` also clears diagnostics\n- Fires `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event with the URI in the change event\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-linter');\nconst diagnostics = [\n    new Diagnostic(range1, \"Error 1\", DiagnosticSeverity.Error),\n    new Diagnostic(range2, \"Warning 1\", DiagnosticSeverity.Warning)\n];\ncollection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n```\n\n#### set(entries: ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): void\n\nReplace diagnostics for multiple resources in this collection.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `entries` (ReadonlyArray<[Uri, readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined]>): An array of tuples where each tuple contains a URI and its diagnostics, or `undefined`\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Multiple tuples of the same URI will be merged. For example, `[[file1, [d1]], [file1, [d2]]]` is equivalent to `[[file1, [d1, d2]]]`\n- If a diagnostics item is `undefined` as in `[file1, undefined]`, all previous diagnostics for that URI are removed but subsequent entries for that URI in the array are still processed\n- Fires `onDidChangeDiagnostics` once with all changed URIs\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.set([\n    [fileUri1, [diagnostic1, diagnostic2]],\n    [fileUri2, [diagnostic3, diagnostic4, diagnostic5]]\n]);\n```\n\n#### delete(uri: Uri): void\n\nRemove all diagnostics from this collection that belong to the provided URI.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri` (Uri): A resource identifier\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Equivalent to `set(uri, undefined)`\n- Fires `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event with the URI\n- If the URI has no diagnostics, nothing happens (no error)\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.delete(document.uri);\n```\n\n#### clear(): void\n\nRemove all diagnostics from this collection across all resources.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Equivalent to calling `set(undefined)` (which is not directly callable but represents the intent)\n- Fires `onDidChangeDiagnostics` event for all previously-diagnosed URIs\n- After clear, the collection is empty\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.clear();\n```\n\n#### forEach(callback: (uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any, thisArg?: any): void\n\nIterate over each entry in this collection.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `callback` (function): Function to execute for each entry with signature `(uri: Uri, diagnostics: readonly Diagnostic[], collection: DiagnosticCollection) => any`\n- `thisArg` (optional): The `this` context used when invoking the handler function\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Called once for each URI that has diagnostics in the collection\n- Iteration order is not guaranteed\n- The callback receives the URI, its diagnostics (immutable array), and a reference to the collection\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncollection.forEach((uri, diagnostics, collection) => {\n    console.log(`${uri.toString()}: ${diagnostics.length} diagnostics`);\n});\n```\n\n#### get(uri: Uri): readonly Diagnostic[] | undefined\n\nGet the diagnostics for a given resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri` (Uri): A resource identifier\n\n**Returns:**\n- An immutable array of Diagnostic objects if diagnostics exist for the URI, or `undefined` if none exist\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns an immutable/readonly array; modifications to the returned array do not affect the collection\n- Returns `undefined` (not an empty array) if no diagnostics exist for the URI\n- Safe to call even if the URI has not been set in the collection\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = collection.get(document.uri);\nif (diagnostics) {\n    console.log(`Found ${diagnostics.length} diagnostics`);\n    for (const diag of diagnostics) {\n        console.log(diag.message);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n#### has(uri: Uri): boolean\n\nCheck if this collection contains diagnostics for a given resource.\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `uri` (Uri): A resource identifier\n\n**Returns:**\n- `true` if the collection has diagnostics for the URI, `false` otherwise\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Does not count zero-width ranges or other special cases\n- Returns `true` even if the diagnostics array is empty (if it was explicitly set)\n- Returns `false` if the URI has never been set or has been cleared\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nif (collection.has(document.uri)) {\n    const diagnostics = collection.get(document.uri);\n    // Process diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n#### dispose(): void\n\nDispose and free associated resources.\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Calls `clear()` internally\n- Removes all diagnostics from the collection\n- After disposal, the collection should not be used\n- Typically called during extension deactivation\n- Fires `onDidChangeDiagnostics` for all previously-diagnosed URIs\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\ncontext.subscriptions.push(collection); // Auto-dispose when extension deactivates\n// Later:\ncollection.dispose(); // Manual disposal\n```\n\n**Iteration:**\n\nDiagnosticCollection implements Iterable, so it can be used with `for...of`:\n\n```typescript\nfor (const [uri, diagnostics] of collection) {\n    console.log(`${uri.toString()}: ${diagnostics.length} issues`);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Functions\n\n### createDiagnosticCollection(name?: string): DiagnosticCollection\n\nCreates a new diagnostic collection.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport function createDiagnosticCollection(name?: string): DiagnosticCollection\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `name` (string, optional): The name of the collection, e.g., 'typescript', 'eslint', 'my-linter'. Used for grouping and filtering in the Problems panel.\n\n**Returns:**\n- A new DiagnosticCollection instance\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Creates an empty collection\n- The collection name is visible in the Problems panel\n- Each extension should typically create one collection per feature or linter\n- Collections are independent; clearing one doesn't affect others\n- Should be stored and disposed in extension lifecycle\n\n**Error Handling:**\n- No errors thrown; even invalid names are accepted (though empty names are not recommended)\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnosticCollection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-extension');\ncontext.subscriptions.push(diagnosticCollection); // Auto-dispose on deactivation\n```\n\n---\n\n### getDiagnostics(resource: Uri): Diagnostic[]\n\nGet all diagnostics for a given resource from all collections.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport function getDiagnostics(resource: Uri): Diagnostic[]\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- `resource` (Uri): A resource URI\n\n**Returns:**\n- An array of Diagnostic objects from all collections for the given resource, or an empty array if none exist\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns diagnostics from ALL diagnostic collections (not just one)\n- Returns an empty array (never undefined) if no diagnostics exist\n- The returned array is a copy, not a reference to internal state\n- Diagnostics are returned in an arbitrary order\n- Includes diagnostics from the built-in collections and all extension collections\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst allDiagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(document.uri);\nconsole.log(`Total diagnostics: ${allDiagnostics.length}`);\n\nfor (const diag of allDiagnostics) {\n    console.log(`${diag.source}: ${diag.message}`);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### getDiagnostics(): [Uri, Diagnostic[]][]\n\nGet all diagnostics from all collections.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport function getDiagnostics(): [Uri, Diagnostic[]][]\n```\n\n**Parameters:**\n- None\n\n**Returns:**\n- An array of tuples, each containing a URI and its associated diagnostics, or an empty array\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Returns diagnostics from ALL collections across ALL resources\n- Returns an empty array (never undefined) if no diagnostics exist\n- The returned array is a copy of internal state\n- Each URI appears at most once in the result\n- Useful for bulk operations or diagnostics overview\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nconst allDiagnosticsEverywhere = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics();\nconsole.log(`Total resources with diagnostics: ${allDiagnosticsEverywhere.length}`);\n\nlet totalDiagnostics = 0;\nfor (const [uri, diagnostics] of allDiagnosticsEverywhere) {\n    totalDiagnostics += diagnostics.length;\n    console.log(`${uri.toString()}: ${diagnostics.length} diagnostics`);\n}\nconsole.log(`Total diagnostics: ${totalDiagnostics}`);\n```\n\n---\n\n## Events\n\n### onDidChangeDiagnostics: Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>\n\nAn event which fires when the global set of diagnostics changes.\n\n**Signature:**\n```typescript\nexport const onDidChangeDiagnostics: Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>\n```\n\n**Type:**\n- `Event<DiagnosticChangeEvent>`\n\n**Event Parameter:**\n- `DiagnosticChangeEvent.uris`: Array of URIs where diagnostics changed\n\n**Behavior:**\n- Fired whenever diagnostics are added, removed, or modified via any DiagnosticCollection\n- Fired once per change operation, even if multiple URIs are affected\n- The event includes only the URIs that changed, not the actual diagnostic content\n- Fired by both the user's collections and built-in collections (TypeScript, etc.)\n- Listeners can query current diagnostics using `getDiagnostics()` if needed\n\n**Usage Notes:**\n- Use this to update UI that depends on the current diagnostics state\n- Avoid expensive operations in event handlers; use debouncing if necessary\n- The event URI list may be empty in some edge cases\n\n**Example:**\n```typescript\nvscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(event => {\n    console.log(`Diagnostics changed for ${event.uris.length} files`);\n\n    for (const uri of event.uris) {\n        const diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n        console.log(`${uri.toString()}: ${diagnostics.length} issues`);\n    }\n});\n```\n\n---\n\n## Usage Examples\n\n### Basic Example: Creating and Publishing Diagnostics\n\nThis example shows how to create a simple linter that validates JSON files:\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    // Create a diagnostic collection\n    const diagnosticCollection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('json-validator');\n    context.subscriptions.push(diagnosticCollection);\n\n    // Listen to document changes\n    vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(event => {\n        const document = event.document;\n\n        // Only validate JSON files\n        if (document.languageId !== 'json') {\n            return;\n        }\n\n        const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n\n        try {\n            JSON.parse(document.getText());\n        } catch (error) {\n            // Create a diagnostic for the parse error\n            const message = error instanceof Error ? error.message : 'Invalid JSON';\n            const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n                new vscode.Range(0, 0, 0, 1),\n                message,\n                vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n            );\n            diagnostic.source = 'json-validator';\n            diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n        }\n\n        // Publish diagnostics for this file\n        diagnosticCollection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n    }, null, context.subscriptions);\n\n    // Clear diagnostics when document is closed\n    vscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(document => {\n        diagnosticCollection.delete(document.uri);\n    }, null, context.subscriptions);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Advanced Example: Multiple Issue Types and Related Information\n\nThis example shows a more sophisticated linter with multiple diagnostic types and related information:\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\ninterface LintIssue {\n    line: number;\n    column: number;\n    length: number;\n    severity: vscode.DiagnosticSeverity;\n    code: string;\n    message: string;\n    relatedInfo?: { line: number; column: number; length: number; message: string };\n}\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    const collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-linter');\n    context.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n    function lintDocument(document: vscode.TextDocument) {\n        const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n        const issues = performLinting(document); // Your custom linting logic\n\n        for (const issue of issues) {\n            const range = new vscode.Range(\n                issue.line, issue.column,\n                issue.line, issue.column + issue.length\n            );\n\n            const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n                range,\n                issue.message,\n                issue.severity\n            );\n            diagnostic.source = 'my-linter';\n            diagnostic.code = {\n                value: issue.code,\n                target: vscode.Uri.parse(`https://docs.example.com/rules/${issue.code}`)\n            };\n\n            // Add related information if available\n            if (issue.relatedInfo) {\n                const relatedRange = new vscode.Range(\n                    issue.relatedInfo.line, issue.relatedInfo.column,\n                    issue.relatedInfo.line, issue.relatedInfo.column + issue.relatedInfo.length\n                );\n                diagnostic.relatedInformation = [\n                    new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n                        new vscode.Location(document.uri, relatedRange),\n                        issue.relatedInfo.message\n                    )\n                ];\n            }\n\n            // Mark unused code\n            if (issue.code === 'unused-var') {\n                diagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\n            }\n\n            diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n        }\n\n        collection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n    }\n\n    // Lint on document open and change\n    vscode.workspace.onDidOpenTextDocument(lintDocument, null, context.subscriptions);\n    vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(event => {\n        lintDocument(event.document);\n    }, null, context.subscriptions);\n\n    // Clean up on close\n    vscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(doc => {\n        collection.delete(doc.uri);\n    }, null, context.subscriptions);\n}\n\nfunction performLinting(document: vscode.TextDocument): LintIssue[] {\n    // Your custom linting implementation\n    return [];\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Real-World Pattern: Throttled Linting with Disposables\n\nThis pattern, used in VS Code's built-in extensions, shows how to handle throttling and proper resource cleanup:\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport class ExtensionLinter {\n    private readonly diagnosticsCollection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection;\n    private readonly disposables: vscode.Disposable[] = [];\n    private lintTimer: NodeJS.Timeout | undefined;\n\n    constructor() {\n        this.diagnosticsCollection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('extension-linter');\n        this.disposables.push(this.diagnosticsCollection);\n\n        // Listen to document changes with debouncing\n        vscode.workspace.onDidChangeTextDocument(\n            event => this.queueLint(event.document),\n            null,\n            this.disposables\n        );\n\n        vscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(\n            document => this.diagnosticsCollection.delete(document.uri),\n            null,\n            this.disposables\n        );\n    }\n\n    private queueLint(document: vscode.TextDocument) {\n        // Clear existing timer\n        if (this.lintTimer) {\n            clearTimeout(this.lintTimer);\n        }\n        // Debounce: wait 300ms after last change before linting\n        this.lintTimer = setTimeout(() => {\n            this.lint(document);\n        }, 300);\n    }\n\n    private async lint(document: vscode.TextDocument) {\n        const diagnostics: vscode.Diagnostic[] = [];\n\n        try {\n            // Perform async linting\n            const issues = await this.lintDocument(document);\n\n            for (const issue of issues) {\n                const diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(\n                    issue.range,\n                    issue.message,\n                    issue.severity\n                );\n                diagnostic.source = 'extension-linter';\n                diagnostics.push(diagnostic);\n            }\n        } catch (error) {\n            console.error('Linting error:', error);\n        }\n\n        // Publish all diagnostics at once\n        this.diagnosticsCollection.set(document.uri, diagnostics);\n    }\n\n    private async lintDocument(document: vscode.TextDocument): Promise<vscode.Diagnostic[]> {\n        // Your linting implementation\n        return [];\n    }\n\n    public dispose() {\n        if (this.lintTimer) {\n            clearTimeout(this.lintTimer);\n        }\n        this.disposables.forEach(d => d.dispose());\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Pattern: Bulk Update with Multiple Files\n\nThis example demonstrates updating diagnostics for multiple files at once:\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport async function runFullProjectLint(\n    collection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection,\n    workspacePath: string\n): Promise<void> {\n    const updates: Array<[vscode.Uri, vscode.Diagnostic[] | undefined]> = [];\n\n    // Scan all files in workspace\n    const files = await vscode.workspace.findFiles('**/*.js');\n\n    for (const fileUri of files) {\n        const document = await vscode.workspace.openTextDocument(fileUri);\n        const diagnostics = await lintFile(document);\n        updates.push([fileUri, diagnostics]);\n    }\n\n    // Apply all updates at once (more efficient than individual set() calls)\n    collection.set(updates);\n}\n\nasync function lintFile(document: vscode.TextDocument): Promise<vscode.Diagnostic[]> {\n    // Your linting implementation\n    return [];\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Pattern: Integration with Code Actions\n\nThis example shows how diagnostics work with Code Actions to provide fixes:\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport class MyCodeActionProvider implements vscode.CodeActionProvider {\n    constructor(private diagnosticsCollection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection) {}\n\n    provideCodeActions(\n        document: vscode.TextDocument,\n        range: vscode.Range | vscode.Selection,\n        context: vscode.CodeActionContext\n    ): vscode.CodeAction[] {\n        const actions: vscode.CodeAction[] = [];\n\n        // Get diagnostics from our collection for this range\n        const diagnostics = this.diagnosticsCollection.get(document.uri) || [];\n\n        for (const diagnostic of diagnostics) {\n            if (!diagnostic.range.intersection(range)) {\n                continue;\n            }\n\n            // Only handle certain codes\n            if (typeof diagnostic.code === 'string' && diagnostic.code === 'unused-var') {\n                const action = new vscode.CodeAction(\n                    'Remove unused variable',\n                    vscode.CodeActionKind.QuickFix\n                );\n                action.diagnostics = [diagnostic];\n\n                const edit = new vscode.WorkspaceEdit();\n                // Apply a fix (simplified example)\n                edit.delete(document.uri, diagnostic.range);\n                action.edit = edit;\n\n                actions.push(action);\n            }\n        }\n\n        return actions;\n    }\n\n    static register(\n        context: vscode.ExtensionContext,\n        diagnosticsCollection: vscode.DiagnosticCollection\n    ): void {\n        const provider = new MyCodeActionProvider(diagnosticsCollection);\n        context.subscriptions.push(\n            vscode.languages.registerCodeActionsProvider(\n                { scheme: 'file', language: 'javascript' },\n                provider\n            )\n        );\n    }\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n### Pattern: Listening to Diagnostic Changes\n\nThis pattern shows how to react to diagnostic changes globally:\n\n```typescript\nimport * as vscode from 'vscode';\n\nexport function activate(context: vscode.ExtensionContext) {\n    // Monitor all diagnostics changes\n    vscode.languages.onDidChangeDiagnostics(event => {\n        for (const uri of event.uris) {\n            const diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\n            const errorCount = diagnostics.filter(\n                d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error\n            ).length;\n            const warningCount = diagnostics.filter(\n                d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning\n            ).length;\n\n            if (errorCount > 0 || warningCount > 0) {\n                console.log(`${uri.toString()}: ${errorCount} errors, ${warningCount} warnings`);\n            }\n        }\n    }, null, context.subscriptions);\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Common Patterns\n\n### Resource Lifecycle Management\n\n**Collection Creation and Disposal:**\n```typescript\n// Create and auto-dispose with context\nconst collection = vscode.languages.createDiagnosticCollection('my-linter');\ncontext.subscriptions.push(collection);\n\n// Later, manual disposal if needed\ncollection.dispose();\n```\n\n**File Cleanup:**\n```typescript\nvscode.workspace.onDidCloseTextDocument(doc => {\n    collection.delete(doc.uri);\n});\n```\n\n### Diagnostic Filtering and Aggregation\n\n**Count diagnostics by severity:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics(uri);\nconst errors = diagnostics.filter(d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Error).length;\nconst warnings = diagnostics.filter(d => d.severity === vscode.DiagnosticSeverity.Warning).length;\n```\n\n**Find all diagnostics in workspace:**\n```typescript\nconst allDiags = vscode.languages.getDiagnostics();\nfor (const [uri, diagnostics] of allDiags) {\n    // Process each URI and its diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n### Batch Updates\n\n**More efficient than multiple set() calls:**\n```typescript\nconst updates: Array<[vscode.Uri, vscode.Diagnostic[] | undefined]> = [];\nfor (const uri of uris) {\n    updates.push([uri, getDiagnosticsFor(uri)]);\n}\ncollection.set(updates);\n```\n\n### Diagnostic Enrichment\n\n**Add metadata and links to diagnostics:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostic = new vscode.Diagnostic(range, message);\ndiagnostic.source = 'my-linter';\ndiagnostic.code = {\n    value: 'E001',\n    target: vscode.Uri.parse('https://example.com/rules/E001')\n};\ndiagnostic.tags = [vscode.DiagnosticTag.Unnecessary];\ndiagnostic.relatedInformation = [\n    new vscode.DiagnosticRelatedInformation(\n        new vscode.Location(uri, relatedRange),\n        'Related issue'\n    )\n];\n```\n\n---\n\n## Error Handling\n\n### Common Error Scenarios\n\n**Invalid Range:**\n- If you provide a Range that extends beyond the document bounds, VS Code will clamp it silently. No error is thrown.\n\n**Invalid URI:**\n- Passing invalid URIs may cause silent failures. Always validate URIs before use.\n\n**Undefined vs Empty Array:**\n- `set(uri, undefined)` clears diagnostics\n- `set(uri, [])` also clears diagnostics\n- `get(uri)` returns `undefined` if no diagnostics exist\n\n**Collection After Dispose:**\n- Using a disposed collection may cause errors or silent failures\n- Always check if the extension is still active before using collections\n\n### Safe Patterns\n\n**Always check before accessing:**\n```typescript\nconst diagnostics = collection.get(uri);\nif (diagnostics && diagnostics.length > 0) {\n    // Safe to iterate\n}\n```\n\n**Handle missing resources gracefully:**\n```typescript\nif (collection.has(uri)) {\n    // Resource has diagnostics\n} else {\n    // Resource has no diagnostics\n}\n```\n\n**Proper cleanup on error:**\n```typescript\ntry {\n    // Perform linting\n    collection.set(uri, diagnostics);\n} catch (error) {\n    console.error('Failed to set diagnostics:', error);\n    collection.delete(uri); // Clean up\n}\n```\n\n---\n\n## Performance Considerations\n\n### Best Practices\n\n1. **Debounce linting**: Use timers to avoid linting on every keystroke\n2. **Batch updates**: Use `set(entries)` instead of multiple `set(uri, ...)` calls\n3. **Lazy linting**: Lint only open files or files with unsaved changes\n4. **Clear unused diagnostics**: Delete diagnostics for closed files promptly\n5. **Limit message length**: Keep diagnostic messages concise to reduce memory usage\n\n### Avoid\n\n- Creating multiple collections for the same linter\n- Linting synchronously on every document change\n- Storing references to diagnostics outside collections\n- Forgetting to dispose collections on deactivation\n\n---\n\n## Related APIs\n\n- **CodeAction**: Used to provide fixes for diagnostics\n- **CodeActionContext**: Includes diagnostics that triggered the code action request\n- **TextDocument**: Source of diagnostic issues\n- **Range**: Specifies the location of a diagnostic\n- **Uri**: Identifies the file associated with a diagnostic\n- **Event**: Used for `onDidChangeDiagnostics` subscription\n\n---\n\n## API Stability\n\nThe Diagnostic API is part of the stable VS Code API and is maintained for backward compatibility. No breaking changes are expected in future releases.\n\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
